Jacob rehearsed how God Almighty had appeared to him and had promised him Abraham’s blessing—innumerable descendants dwelling in the land . . . as an everlasting possession (cp. [28:10–22](https://ref.ly/Gen28:10-Gen28:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:3–GEN 48:4

## Genesis 48:5–7 (id: 12895)

Jacob, prompted by his memory of Rachel (see [35:16–20](https://ref.ly/Gen35:16-Gen35:20)), blessed Joseph by elevating his two sons as coheirs with his other sons—the tribes of Ephraim and Manasseh would have shares along with the other tribes that came from Jacob (see [Josh 16–17](https://ref.ly/Josh16:1-Josh17:18)). Jacob also gave Ephraim, Joseph’s younger son, the birthright (see [1 Chr 5:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:1-1Chr5:2)). As a result of this blessing, Ephraim and Manasseh became large and powerful tribes (see [Josh 17:14–18](https://ref.ly/Josh17:14-Josh17:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:5–GEN 48:7

## Genesis 48:10 (id: 12889)

As Isaac his father had done, Jacob now gave the blessing when his eyesight was failing (cp. [27:1](https://ref.ly/Gen27:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:10

## Genesis 48:14 (id: 12890)

The right hand was for the head of the firstborn, and Jacob was deliberately giving that position to the younger son. That pattern was followed for four consecutive generations: Isaac over Ishmael, Jacob over Esau, Joseph over Reuben, and Ephraim over Manasseh. Many years later, Ephraim became the leading tribe in the northern kingdom, superior to the tribe of Manasseh. The entire northern kingdom of Israel was occasionally called Ephraim (see study notes on 2 Chr 28:12; Isa 11:13; Ezek 37:15–28; Hos 6:4; Zech 9:10).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:14
* **Associated Articles:** Ezekiel 37:15-28 (ID: `11764@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Hosea 6:4 (ID: `13462@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Isaiah 11:13 (ID: `15841@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Zechariah 9:10 (ID: `26133@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Genesis 48:15–16 (id: 12891)

In his blessing on Joseph, Jacob used a threefold invocation to describe the God in whom he trusted: (1\) the God who was in covenant with his fathers Abraham and Isaac ([28:13](https://ref.ly/Gen28:13); [31:5](https://ref.ly/Gen31:5), [42](https://ref.ly/Gen31:42); [32:9](https://ref.ly/Gen32:9); [46:3](https://ref.ly/Gen46:3)); (2\) the God who had been his shepherd (cp. [49:24](https://ref.ly/Gen49:24); [Exod 6:6](https://ref.ly/Exod6:6); [Ps 23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1); [Isa 59:20](https://ref.ly/Isa59:20)); and (3\) the Angel who rescued him from all harm. He prayed the same blessings for Joseph’s sons.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:15–GEN 48:16

## Genesis 48:17–19 (id: 12892)

Joseph was upset: He expected God to act according to convention, but faith recognizes that God’s ways are not man’s ways, and God’s thoughts are not man’s thoughts. It took Jacob a lifetime to learn this lesson, but he did learn it, and here he acted on it.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:17–GEN 48:19

## Genesis 48:22 (id: 12893)

Joseph was later buried at Shechem ([Josh 24:32](https://ref.ly/Josh24:32)) as a sign that he possessed this bequeathed extra portion (Hebrew shekem) of land. Jacob had apparently conquered this area though the occasion is not mentioned elsewhere.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 48:22

## Genesis 49:1–2 (id: 12897)

Jacob’s words were deliberately chosen prophetic oracles. The days to come refer to the conquest and settlement of the Promised Land, and beyond that to the messianic age. They would all share in the blessing; all the tribes would enter the land with Joshua, but they would not all participate equally.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:1–GEN 49:2

## Genesis 49:1–28 (id: 12896)

Jacob, by faith and as God’s spokesman, looked forward to Israel’s settlement in the land, and beyond that to the glorious future. Here at the end of the patriarchal age, he foretold what would happen to each tribe as he evaluated his sons one by one, just as Noah had done at the end of the primeval era (cp. [9:25–27](https://ref.ly/Gen9:25-Gen9:27)). The character and acts of each ancestor affected the lives of his descendants ([Exod 20:5–6](https://ref.ly/Exod20:5-Exod20:6); [34:6–7](https://ref.ly/Exod34:6-Exod34:7); [Num 14:18](https://ref.ly/Num14:18); [Jer 32:18](https://ref.ly/Jer32:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:1–GEN 49:28

## Genesis 49:3–4 (id: 12914)

As firstborn, Reuben was entitled to be head of the family, but because he had the ungoverned impulses of boiling or turbulent waters ([35:22](https://ref.ly/Gen35:22)), Jacob prophesied that Reuben would fail in leadership (see [37:21–22](https://ref.ly/Gen37:21-Gen37:22), [29](https://ref.ly/Gen37:29); [42:22](https://ref.ly/Gen42:22), [37–38](https://ref.ly/Gen42:37-Gen42:38); cp. [Judg 5:15–16](https://ref.ly/Judg5:15-Judg5:16); [1 Chr 5:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:1-1Chr5:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:3–GEN 49:4

## Genesis 49:5–7 (id: 12916)

Simeon and Levi were violent and lawless; instead of serving justice, they indulged their uncontrolled anger and disregarded life ([34:24–29](https://ref.ly/Gen34:24-Gen34:29)). • I will scatter them: Simeon’s land was largely absorbed into Judah’s ([Josh 19:1](https://ref.ly/Josh19:1), [9](https://ref.ly/Josh19:9)); Levi was given a more honorable future because the Levites became the priestly tribe (see [Exod 32:25–29](https://ref.ly/Exod32:25-Exod32:29)), but they had no region of their own ([Josh 21](https://ref.ly/Josh21:1-Josh21:45)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:5–GEN 49:7

## Genesis 49:8–12 (id: 12917)

The blessing on Judah commands the most attention. In this oracle, Jacob predicted the fierce, lion\-like dominance of Judah over his enemies and over his brothers, who would praise him (cp. [29:35](https://ref.ly/Gen29:35); see, e.g., [Ruth 4:11–12](https://ref.ly/Ruth4:11-Ruth4:12); [1 Sam 18:6–7](https://ref.ly/1Sam18:6-1Sam18:7); [Pss 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12), [45](https://ref.ly/Ps45:1-Ps45:17), [72](https://ref.ly/Ps72:1-Ps72:20); [Isa 11:1–13](https://ref.ly/Isa11:1-Isa11:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:8–GEN 49:12

## Genesis 49:10 (id: 12898)

This verse anticipates the kingship in Judah (cp. [17:6](https://ref.ly/Gen17:6), [16](https://ref.ly/Gen17:16); [35:11](https://ref.ly/Gen35:11)). Although the birthright blessing went to Joseph, Judah would provide Israel’s rulers (see [1 Chr 5:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:1-1Chr5:2)). A long line of kings from Judah would retain the scepter, the symbol of rule; the last king would be the one to whom it belongs, the promised Messiah (see [2 Sam 7:4–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:4-2Sam7:16); [Pss 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12), [45](https://ref.ly/Ps45:1-Ps45:17), [60](https://ref.ly/Ps60:1-Ps60:12); [Isa 11](https://ref.ly/Isa11:1-Isa11:16); [Ezek 21:26–27](https://ref.ly/Ezek21:26-Ezek21:27); [Zech 9:9](https://ref.ly/Zech9:9); [Rev 5:5](https://ref.ly/Rev5:5)). • from his descendants: Literally *from between his feet,* a poetic euphemism for reproductive organs. • until the coming of the one to whom it belongs (Or *until tribute is brought to him and the peoples obey;* traditionally rendered *until Shiloh comes*): These differences arise from ambiguities in the Hebrew text. Rule of Israel belongs to Judah’s descendant through David’s line ([2 Sam 7:8–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:8-2Sam7:16)), and he will eventually rule all nations, as signified by the bringing of *tribute* (see [Pss 68:29](https://ref.ly/Ps68:29); [72:8–11](https://ref.ly/Ps72:8-Ps72:11); [Isa 2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4); [Eph 4:8–10](https://ref.ly/Eph4:8-Eph4:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:10

## Genesis 49:11–12 (id: 12899)

These descriptions envision the abundance of the Messiah’s kingdom (see [Isa 61:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa61:6-Isa61:7); [65:21–25](https://ref.ly/Isa65:21-Isa65:25); [Zech 3:10](https://ref.ly/Zech3:10)). When the Messiah comes, there will be paradise\-like splendor and abundance on the earth. • He ties his foal to a grapevine: Grapevines will be so abundant that they will be used for hitching posts, and wine will be as abundant as fresh water (see [Amos 9:13–14](https://ref.ly/Amos9:13-Amos9:14); [Zech 3:10](https://ref.ly/Zech3:10)). • The coming one will have eyes . . . darker than wine and teeth . . . whiter than milk: He will be vigorous and healthy, as will be the era of his rule. Jesus’ miracle of changing water into wine ([John 2:1–12](https://ref.ly/John2:1-John2:12)), his first sign, was an announcement that the Messiah had come; it was a foretaste of even better things to come.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:11–GEN 49:12

## Genesis 49:13 (id: 12900)

The oracle said Zebulun would dwell by the sea and be a safe harbor, but in the actual settlement they spread inland (see [Josh 19:10–16](https://ref.ly/Josh19:10-Josh19:16)). The oracle did not give specific borders for the tribes.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:13

## Genesis 49:14–15 (id: 12901)

Like a sturdy donkey, the tribe of Issachar would be forced to work for others. Issachar was often subjugated by invading armies.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:14–GEN 49:15

## Genesis 49:16–17 (id: 12902)

Dan was called to provide justice (*Dan* means “judge”), but the tribe would choose treachery, like a snake beside the road (see [Judg 18](https://ref.ly/Judg18:1-Judg18:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:16–GEN 49:17

## Genesis 49:18 (id: 12903)

At this point, Jacob interjected an expression of hope. He may have been indirectly reminding his sons of their need for dependence on the Lord or expressing his hope in the Messiah’s reign, when he and his descendants would be rescued from all trouble, grief, and human treachery.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:18

## Genesis 49:19 (id: 12904)

Three of the six Hebrew words in this verse are wordplays on the name Gad (“attack”). Gad will be attacked by marauding bands (attackers), but he will attack. The tribes that settled east of the Jordan River frequently experienced border raids (see [Josh 13](https://ref.ly/Josh13:1-Josh13:33); [2 Kgs 10:32–33](https://ref.ly/2Kgs10:32-2Kgs10:33); [1 Chr 5:18–19](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:18-1Chr5:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:19

## Genesis 49:20 (id: 12905)

Asher would be fertile and productive, providing rich foods. The tribe settled along the rich northern coast of Canaan.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:20

## Genesis 49:21 (id: 12906)

Naphtali, like a doe, would be a free mountain people (cp. [Judg 5:18](https://ref.ly/Judg5:18)). The tribe settled in the hilly region northwest of the Sea of Galilee.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:21

## Genesis 49:22–26 (id: 12907)

This oracle treats Joseph more expansively than any of the others, for here the main blessing lay (see [1 Chr 5:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:1-1Chr5:2)). Jacob lavished promises of victory and prosperity on Joseph’s two tribes. Ephraimites recorded as victorious in battle include Joshua ([Josh 6](https://ref.ly/Josh6:1-Josh6:27), [8](https://ref.ly/Josh8:1-Josh8:35), [10](https://ref.ly/Josh10:1-Josh10:43), [12](https://ref.ly/Josh12:1-Josh12:24)) and Deborah ([Judg 4](https://ref.ly/Judg4:1-Judg4:24)). Victorious descendants of Manasseh include Gideon ([Judg 6–8](https://ref.ly/Judg6:1-Judg8:35)) and Jephthah ([Judg 11:1–12:7](https://ref.ly/Judg11:1-Judg12:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:22–GEN 49:26

## Genesis 49:24–26 (id: 12908)

Five names for God introduce five blessings; God is the giver of all good things.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:24–GEN 49:26

## Genesis 49:25 (id: 12909)

The blessings of the heavens above meant rain for crops. • The blessings of the watery depths were streams and wells of water. • The blessings of the breasts and womb were abundant offspring.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:25

## Genesis 49:26 (id: 12910)

Joseph . . . is a prince among his brothers: a reflection of both his character and his position.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:26

## Genesis 49:27 (id: 12911)

The oracle about Benjamin describes a violent tribe (see [Judg 20](https://ref.ly/Judg20:1-Judg20:48); [1 Sam 9:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Sam9:1-1Sam9:2); [19:10](https://ref.ly/1Sam19:10); [22:17](https://ref.ly/1Sam22:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:27

## Genesis 49:28 (id: 12912)

These prophecies are broad in scope, foretelling the future of the different tribes in general terms. Individuals, by faith and obedience, could find great blessing from God regardless of what happened to their clan.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:28

## Genesis 49:29–33 (id: 12913)

Bury me with my father: This grave in the land of Canaan represented hope for the future (cp. [47:29–30](https://ref.ly/Gen47:29-Gen47:30)). Others buried at the cave of Machpelah near Hebron were Sarah ([23:19](https://ref.ly/Gen23:19)), Abraham ([25:7–9](https://ref.ly/Gen25:7-Gen25:9)), Isaac ([35:27–29](https://ref.ly/Gen35:27-Gen35:29)), Rebekah, and Leah.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:29–GEN 49:33

## Genesis 49:33 (id: 12915)

Jacob died at the age of 147 ([47:28](https://ref.ly/Gen47:28)), bringing his life of struggle and sorrow to an end. Jacob had always had an unquenchable desire for God’s blessing. He had a deep piety that habitually relied on God despite all else. In the end, he died a man of genuine faith. He learned where real blessings come from, and through his faith would be able to hand these on to his sons ([Heb 11:21](https://ref.ly/Heb11:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 49:33

## Genesis 50:1–6 (id: 12929)

As with his father and grandfather, Jacob’s death brought the end of an era.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:1–GEN 50:6

## Genesis 50:2 (id: 12937)

Jacob’s body was embalmed for burial in typical Egyptian fashion.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:2

## Genesis 50:3 (id: 12938)

the Egyptians mourned for Jacob for seventy days, just two days short of the mourning period for a pharaoh. This showed the great respect that the Egyptians had for Joseph.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:3

## Genesis 50:4–6 (id: 12939)

Joseph needed Pharaoh’s permission to leave his post temporarily to bury his father in Canaan. Pharaoh readily granted this freedom to the former slave.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:4–GEN 50:6

## Genesis 50:7–9 (id: 12940)

This was Joseph’s first return to his homeland in thirty\-nine years. The trip was temporary. Centuries later, the family of Israel would permanently leave Egypt, taking Joseph’s bones with them for burial in the land of promise (see [50:25](https://ref.ly/Gen50:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:7–GEN 50:9

## Genesis 50:10–13 (id: 12930)

This journey into Canaan was made in sorrow to bury a man; the next journey into the land would be to live there.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:10–GEN 50:13

## Genesis 50:15–18 (id: 12931)

The brothers pleaded for Joseph’s forgiveness, referring to themselves as Joseph’s slaves (cp. [37:7](https://ref.ly/Gen37:7); [44:16](https://ref.ly/Gen44:16), [33](https://ref.ly/Gen44:33)). The brothers were afraid that Joseph’s earlier reconciliation with them had been motivated only by his desire to see his father again. With neither Jacob nor Pharaoh to restrain him, they feared that he might now take revenge on them. But Joseph . . . wept because they still feared reprisal.

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:15–GEN 50:18

## Genesis 50:19–21 (id: 12932)

Joseph reassured his brothers that God planned to fulfill the promised blessing (cp. [45:5](https://ref.ly/Gen45:5), [7–9](https://ref.ly/Gen45:7-Gen45:9)), and he promised kindness and provision (cp. [45:11](https://ref.ly/Gen45:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:19–GEN 50:21

## Genesis 50:22–23 (id: 12933)

Joseph lived to see his great\-great\-grandchildren by Ephraim, and his great\-grandchildren by Manasseh—a sign of God’s blessing (see [Ps 128:6](https://ref.ly/Ps128:6); [Prov 17:6](https://ref.ly/Prov17:6); [Isa 53:10](https://ref.ly/Isa53:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:22–GEN 50:23

## Genesis 50:23 (id: 12934)

whom he claimed as his own (literally *who were born on Joseph’s knees*): Placing them on his knees at their birth was a symbolic act signifying that they came from him and belonged to him (cp. [Job 3:12](https://ref.ly/Job3:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:23

## Genesis 50:24–25 (id: 12935)

God will surely come to help you (literally *visit you*): These words of Joseph, given twice, summarize the hope expressed throughout both the Old Testament and the New Testament. God’s visitation in the person of the Messiah, the offspring of Abraham, would bring the curse to an end and establish the long\-awaited blessing of God in a new creation. The company of the faithful would wait in expectation for that to happen. • Like his father before him, Joseph made his brothers promise that his bones would be taken out of Egypt when God would come to take them (to help you and lead you back) to Canaan (see [Exod 13:19](https://ref.ly/Exod13:19); [Josh 24:32](https://ref.ly/Josh24:32); [Heb 11:22](https://ref.ly/Heb11:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:24–GEN 50:25

## Genesis 50:26 (id: 12936)

Joseph’s death signified the end of his generation (see study notes on 25:7–8; 35:1–29) and of the patriarchal age. From this point forward, God dealt with Israel as a nation. • Joseph’s body was kept in Egypt as a pledge of hope for slaves awaiting the Promised Land (see [Exod 13:19](https://ref.ly/Exod13:19); [Heb 11:39–40](https://ref.ly/Heb11:39-Heb11:40)). He was eventually buried in Shechem (see [Josh 24:32](https://ref.ly/Josh24:32)), where Jacob had originally sent him ([Gen 37:13](https://ref.ly/Gen37:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** GEN 50:26
* **Associated Articles:** Genesis 25:7-8 (ID: `12527@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Genesis 35:1-29 (ID: `12690@TyndaleStudyNotes`)
